         <h3>Route-Book</h3>
         <h3>Buffalo Bill's Wild West</h3>
         <h3>Season 1899.</h3>
      </div>

      <span class="hr"> </span>
      <span class="pageimage">
         <a href="large/wfc.route.1899.002.jpg"
            rel="prettyPhoto[pp_gal]"
            title="&lt;a href=&#34;large/wfc.route.1899.002.jpg&#34; target=&#34;_blank&#34; &gt;open image in new window&lt;/a&gt;">

         </a>
      </span>

      <div class="letter doublespace ">

         <div class="note">Handwritten</div>


         <span class="dateline">New York, Oct 19th.</span>
         <span class="salute">To whom it may Concern</span>


         <p>To any officer U. S Army to knows W. F. Cody (Buffalo Bill) or myself. Langdon is a good boy a Rooseveltean and a thoroughbred with all the ambitions of the true soldier.</p>
         <span class="closer">
            <br/>John M Burke</span>

         <div class="note">End handwritten text</div>
      </div>

      <h6 class="fw">20</h6>

   </div>

   <span class="hr"> </span>
   <span class="pageimage">
      <a href="large/wfc.route.1899.026.jpg"
         rel="prettyPhoto[pp_gal]"
         title="&lt;a href=&#34;large/wfc.route.1899.026.jpg&#34; target=&#34;_blank&#34; &gt;open image in new window&lt;/a&gt;">
         <img src="thumbnails/wfc.route.1899.026.jpg" class="display &#xA;            "/>
      </a>
   </span>

   <div class=" doublespace ">
      <h3>Official Programme.</h3>

      <p>1—Overture, "Star Spangled Banner," Cowboy Band, Wm. Sweeney, Leader.</p>

      <p>2—Grand Review, introducing the Rough Riders of the World—Indians, Cowboys, Mexicans, Cossacks, Gauchos, Arabs, Scouts, Guides and detachments of fully-equipped Regular Soldiers of the Armies of America, England, Germany and Russia, a Color Guard of Cuban Veterans, and a squad of Hawaiian, Porto Rican and Filipino Rough Riders.</p>

      <p>3—Miss Annie Oakley, Celebrated Shot, who will illustrate her dexterity in the use of firearms.</p>

      <p>4—Race of Races. Race between a Cowboy, a Cossack, a Mexican, an Arab, a Gaucho, and an Indian, on Spanish-Mexican, Bronco, Russian, Indian and Arabian Horses.</p>

      <p>5—U. S. Artillery Drill, by veterans from Capt. Thorpe's Battery D, Fifth Regiment. U. S. Artillery.</p>

      <p>6—Illustrating a Prairie Emigrant Train Crossing the Plains. It is attacked by marauding Indians, who are in turn repulsed by "Buffalo Bill" and a number of Scouts and Cowboys.</p>

      <p>7—Pony Express. A former Pony Post Rider will show how letters and telegrams of the Republic were distributed across our Continent previous to the building of railways and telegraph.</p>

      <p>8—A Group of Mexicans from Old Mexico will illustrate the use of the lasso and perform various feats of horsemanship.</p>

      <p>9—The Battle of San Juan Hill. Introducing detachments from Roosevelt's Rough Riders, Twenty-fourth Infantry, Ninth and Tenth Cavalry, Grimes' Battery, Garcia's Cuban Scouts, Pack Train, etc., etc.<br/>
Scene 1—A halt on the Road to San Juan.<br/>
(Several hours are supposed to elapse before the opening of the second scene.)<br/>
Scene 2—Storming the Hill.</p>

      <h6 class="fw">21</h6>

      <span class="hr"> </span>
      <span class="pageimage">
         <a href="large/wfc.route.1899.027.jpg"
            rel="prettyPhoto[pp_gal]"
            title="&lt;a href=&#34;large/wfc.route.1899.027.jpg&#34; target=&#34;_blank&#34; &gt;open image in new window&lt;/a&gt;">
            <img src="thumbnails/wfc.route.1899.027.jpg" class="display &#xA;            "/>
         </a>
      </span>

      <p>10—A Group of Riffian Arab Horsemen will illustrate their style of horsemanship, together with native sports and pastimes.</p>

      <p>11—Johnny Baker, Celebrated Young American Marksman.</p>

      <p>12—Cossacks, from the Caucasus of Russia, in feats of horsemanship, native dances, etc.</p>

      <p>13—Gymkana Race. Riders gallop, dismount, turn coat inside out, remount, gallop, dismount, light cigar, put up umbrella, mount and come in with unbrella up and cigar lighted.</p>

      <p>14—Cowboy Fun. Picking objects from the ground, lassoing wild horses, riding the buckers, etc.</p>

      <p>15—Indians from the Sioux, Arapahoe, Brulé and Cheyenne tribes will illustrate the Indian mode of fighting, war dances and games.</p>

      <p>16—Military Musical Drill, by a detachment from the 16th Lancers (Queen's Own), British Army, and a detachment from the Garde-Kürassiers of His Majesty Kaiser Wilhelm II.</p>

      <p>17—Sixth United States Cavalry. Veterans from Col. Sumner's celebrated regiment at Ft. Meyer, Va., in military exercises, and an exhibition of athletic sports and horsemanship.</p>

      <div class="note">Note.—The men will wear the uniforms adopted by the United States Army on the frontier. The horses are Western range horses, used in this manner for the first time in history. The Army and National Guard use the "American" horse.</div>

      <p>18—Attack on the Deadwood Mail-Coach by Indians, repulse of the Indians, and rescue of the stage, passengers and mail, by "Buffalo Bill" and his attendant Cowboys.</p>

      <p>19—Racing by Indian Boys on Bareback Horses.</p>

      <h6 class="fw">22</h6>

      <span class="hr"> </span>
      <span class="pageimage">
         <a href="large/wfc.route.1899.028.jpg"
            rel="prettyPhoto[pp_gal]"
            title="&lt;a href=&#34;large/wfc.route.1899.028.jpg&#34; target=&#34;_blank&#34; &gt;open image in new window&lt;/a&gt;">
            <img src="thumbnails/wfc.route.1899.028.jpg" class="display &#xA;            "/>
         </a>
      </span>

      <p>20—Three Minutes With the Rough Riders of the World.</p>

      <p>21—Col. W. F. Cody ("Buffalo Bill") in his unique feats of sharpshooting while riding at full speed.</p>

      <p>22—Buffalo Hunt, as it was in the Far West of North America, by "Buffalo Bill" and Indians exhibiting the last of the only known native herd of buffalo.</p>

      <p>23—Attack on Settlers' Cabin and rescue by "Buffalo Bill" and a band of Cowboys, Scouts and Frontiersmen.</p>

      <p>24—Salute, by the entire company.</p>
   </div>

   <div class=" doublespace ">
      <h3>The Annual Spring Opening.</h3>

      <p>The show was moved from "Ambrose Park" to Madison Square Garden for the opening of the season on Sunday, March 26th. The parade which was to have taken place on Tuesday, 28th, had to be postponed until the following day on account of inclement weather.</p>

      <p>The first performance was given on Wednesday night, March 29th, before a crowded house. Several entirely new features were introduced in the programme, the chief being "The Battle of San Juan," which proved an instantaneous success.</p>

      <p>On Friday, April 7th, the afternoon performance was given for the benefit of the orphans and inmates of the different asylums and institutions around New York. Altogether, thirty-one performances were given during the stay in the Garden, at each of which the Garden was well filled, while on several occasions the doors had to be closed for the night performance. The season proved the most successful ever given in New York.</p>

      <h6 class="fw">23</h6>

   <div class=" doublespace ">
      <h6 class="fw">April</h6>

      <div class=" ">
         <h4>Mon. 17 and Tues. 18</h4>
         <h4>Baltimore, Md.</h4>
         <h4>P. R. R. 186.</h4>
         <p>The trains, with the canvas, seats, etc., reached here Saturday morning. The show opened under canvas, in fine, warm weather, giving four performances to crowded houses. Harry Skeen, for several seasons our car repairer, died suddenly in the hospital here. Cowboy Nelson goes to the hospital with a bad case of blood poisoning.</p>
         <p>Lot—York Road and Oxford Avenue.</p>
         <p>Arena—195 x 363.</p>
      </div>

      <div class=" ">
         <h4>Wed. 19 and Thurs. 20</h4>
         <h4>Washington, D. C.—P. R. R. 43.</h4>
         <p>Arrived 6.30 A. M., a slight accident to first section having delayed us two hours. Weather warm and clear. Four performances were given here, at each of which the tent was crowded.</p>
         <p>Lot—N Capitol and "M" Street.</p>
         <p>Arena—200 x 303.</p>
      </div>

      <div class=" ">
         <h4>Fri. 21</h4>
         <h4>Richmond, Va.</h4>
         <h4>P. R. R. and R., F. &amp; P. 116.</h4>
         <p>Arrived 7.30 A. M. Half-mile haul to lot. Weather clear; big business at both performances.</p>
         <p>Lot—Fair Gounds.</p>
         <p>Arena—179 x 375.</p>
      </div>

      <div class=" ">
         <h4>Sat. 22</h4>
         <h4>Staunton, Va.</h4>
         <h4>C. &amp; O. 136.</h4>
         <p>Arrived 8.00 A. M. One-mile haul to lot. Weather clear; attendance big in afternoon, light in evening.</p>
         <p>Lot—Opposite Fair Grounds.</p>
         <p>Arena—156 x 331.</p>
      </div>

      <h6 class="fw">April.</h6>
      <div class=" ">
         <h4>Mon. 24</h4>
         <h4>Lynchburg, Va.</h4>
         <h4>C. &amp; O. 141.</h4>
         <p>The show did not reach town till 11.00 A. M. Flat cars were transferred to siding near lot, to avoid the long haul. Franz gets a fall, and is bruised up a little. Weather clear; business big.</p>
         <p>Lot—5th Street, opp. City Park.</p>
         <p>Arena—169 x 346.</p>
      </div>

      <div class=" ">
         <h4>Tues. 25</h4>
         <h4>Roanoke, Va.</h4>
         <h4>N. &amp; W. 53.</h4>
         <p>Arrived 7.30 A. M. Lot about one mile from crossing. In spite of a steady rain, tent was well filled at both performances.</p>
         <p>Lot—Jefferson Street.</p>
         <p>Arena—160 x 349.</p>
      </div>

      <div class=" ">
         <h4>Wed. 26</h4>
         <h4>Bluefield, W. Va.</h4>
         <h4>N. &amp; W. 107.</h4>
         <p>Only one performance was given here, owing to long run to next stand. The road to the lot was in very bad condition, and gave us a lot of extra work. Weather cloudy; rain at night; business very big.</p>
         <p>Lot—Bland Street.</p>
         <p>Arena—147 x 320.</p>
      </div>

      <div class=" ">
         <h4>Thur. 27</h4>
         <h4>Bristol, Tenn.</h4>
         <h4>N. &amp; W. 169.</h4>
         <p>Arrived in three sections; first section did not get in till 12.30. One performance only, to big business.</p>
         <p>Lot—Scranton and Sullins streets.</p>
         <p>Arena—160 x 367.</p>
      </div>

      <div class=" ">
         <h4>Fri. 28</h4>
         <h4>Knoxville, Tenn.</h4>
         <h4>Southern. 135.</h4>
         <p>Arrived early. Lot very dusty. Weather warn and clear; big business afternoon and night.</p>
         <p>Lot—Bell Avenue and Bell Street.</p>
         <p>Arena—174 x 376.</p>
      </div>

      <div class=" ">
         <h4>Sat. 29</h4>
         <h4>Chattanooga, Tenn.</h4>
         <h4>Southern. 111.</h4>
         <p>A broken axle on flat car delayed the second section five hours. Weather clear; business light. Frank Ackie, an eight-horse driver, died suddenly of heart failure.</p>
         <p>Lot—Rossville and Montgomery aves.</p>
         <p>Arena—160 x 376.</p>
      </div>

         <h4>N. C. &amp; St. L. 151.</h4>
         <p>Arrived 10.30 A. M. Two-mile haul to lot, which was in good condition. Weather very warm; large attendance at both performances.</p>
         <p>Lot—Broad and Spring.</p>
         <p>Arena—163 x 393.</p>

         <p>Lot—8th Street.</p>
         <p>Arena—183 x 382.</p>

         <h4>L. &amp; N. 114.</h4>
         <p>Arrived 8.00 A. M. Three-mile haul to lot; afternoon attendance very large, fair at night; weather warm and clear.</p>
         <p>Lot—Jackson and Oak streets.</p>
         <p>Arena—189 x 394.</p>

         <h4>P., C., C. &amp; St. L. 110.</h4>

         <p>Lot—Fair Grounds.</p>
         <p>Arena—157 x 334.</p>

         <p>Lot—W. Washington Street.</p>
         <p>Arena—161 x 377.</p>
      </div>

      <div class=" ">
         <h4>Sat. 6</h4>
         <h4>Richmond, Ind.</h4>
         <h4>P., C., C. &amp; St. L. 68.</h4>
         <p>Weather cloudy with rain at night. Lot very rough. T. J. McManus, a canvasman, fell from a wagon while leaving the lot and was instantly killed.</p>
         <p>Lot—N. "F" and 19th Street.</p>
         <p>Arena—164 x 341.</p>

      <h6 class="fw">May.</h6>

      <div class=" ">
         <h4>Mon. 8 and Tues. 9</h4>
         <h4>Cincinnati, O.</h4>
         <h4>P., C., C. &amp; St. L. 74.</h4>
         <p>The first day here the rain kept the lot in very bad condition, and had a noticeable effect on the attendance. Tuesday, the weather cleared and the tent was crowded twice. During the night performance, the roof of an old pavilion gave way under the weight of three or four hundred rubbers, and several were seriously hurt. F. J. Healy of U. S. Cavalry detachment closes.</p>
         <p>Lot—Dodsworth and Coleraine aves.</p>
         <p>Arena—160 x 384.</p>
      </div>

      <div class=" ">
         <h4>Wed. 10</h4>
         <h4>Dayton, O.</h4>
         <h4>C., H. &amp; D. 59.</h4>
         <p>Arrived in town early. Weather cloudy; business good. Cowboy Tom Hunter has a fall from a bucker and is badly shaken up. Wittman of U. S. Cavalry fell and received several cuts and bruises.</p>
         <p>Lot—Fair Grounds.</p>
         <p>Arena—183 x 382.</p>
      </div>

      <div class=" ">
         <h4>Thurs. 11</h4>
         <h4>Springfiled, O.</h4>
         <h4>C., C., C. &amp; St. L. 24.</h4>
         <p>Arrived about 4.00 A. M. Weather clear and warm; two good houses. Mike Quinlan is sent to the hospital, with a bad cut in the leg.</p>
         <p>Lot—Fair Grounds.</p>
         <p>Arena—166 x 385.</p>
      </div>

      <div class=" ">
         <h4>Fri. 12</h4>
         <h4>Columbus, O.</h4>
         <h4>C., C., C. &amp; St. L. 43.</h4>
         <p>Arrived early. Very long haul to lot. Weather cloudy with rain. Lot very muddy; good business in spite of weather. Jas. Anderson, our former superintendent, pays us a visit.</p>
         <p>Lot—Livingstone and Lynwood aves.</p>
         <p>Arena—196 x 391.</p>
      </div>

      <div class=" ">
         <h4>Sat. 13</h4>
         <h4>Newark, O.</h4>
         <h4>P., C., C. &amp; St. L. 33.</h4>
         <p>Weather, rain during afternoon; business fair. While the artillery detachment was going into action No 2 turned completely over, Pony Moore got his shoulder broken, Hudson, Davis and Triangle were badly cut and bruised.</p>
         <p>Lot—11th and Church streets.</p>
         <p>Arena—171 x 334.</p>
      </div>

         <h4>Pittsburg, Pa.</h4>
         <h4>P., C., C. &amp; St. L. 165.</h4>
         <p>Arrived at noon Sunday. Weather clear; very large attendance the first day, the doors being closed at evening performance. Pony Moore leaves for New York to doctor broken shoulder. The show was packed during a heavy thunderstorm Tuesday evening.</p>
         <p>Lot—Exhibition Park, Allegheny.</p>
         <p>Arena—200 x 378.</p>

         <h4>P. R. R. 132.</h4>
         <p>Arrived 11 A. M., having been delayed by wrecks along the line. A heavy rain puts the lot in such bad condition that the night performance is abandoned; attendance very light.</p>
         <p>Lot—Washington Avenue.</p>
         <p>Arena—166 x 343.</p>
      </div>

         <h4>Williamsport, Pa.</h4>
         <h4>P. R. R. 79.</h4>
         <p>Arrived early, one-mile haul to lot. The bad weather stays with us, but the tent was well filled at both performances.</p>
         <p>Lot—Brandon Ave. and Cherry St.</p>
         <p>Arena—159 x 336.</p>

         <p>Lot—West Side Driving Park.</p>
         <p>Arena—165 x 365.</p>
      </div>

         <h4>L. V. 78.</h4>
         <p>Arrived early. Lot situated on top of steep hill. Weather very cold; attendance light. Frank 
Eldredge, a four-horse driver, was severely hurt, by being thrown from seat of wagon.</p>
         <p>Lot—Charles Street.</p>
         <p>Arena—147 x 303.</p>

         <h4>Mon. 22</h4>
         <h4>Scranton, Pa.</h4>
         <h4>L. V. and C. of N. J. 96.</h4>
         <p>Weather cleared, and a bright, warm day brings out a large crowd, making it necessary to close the doors on the afternoon performance. Frank Eldredge, the driver who was hurt in Towanda, was taken to the hospital here.</p>
         <p>Lot—Ash Street and Wyoming Avenue.</p>
         <p>Arena—168 x 369.</p>

      <div class=" ">
         <h4>Tues. 23</h4>
         <h4>Easton, Pa.</h4>
         <h4>C. of N. J. 119.</h4>
         <p>Weather clear, a light shower during afternoon; big business at both performances. Visits are exchanged with the "La Pearl" show, playing at South Bethlehem, twelve miles from here.</p>
         <p>Lot—Northampton and 12th streets.</p>
         <p>Arena—160 x 346.</p>
      </div>

         <h4>C. of N. J. 17.</h4>
         <p>Arrived early, everything being ready by 9.00 A. M. Weather clear; attendance big at both performances.</p>
         <p>Lot—Fair Grounds.</p>
         <p>Arena—166 x 349.</p>
      </div>

      <div class=" ">
         <h4>Thur. 25</h4>
         <h4>Pottsville, Pa.</h4>
         <h4>P. &amp; R. 71.</h4>
         <p>Arrived 6.30 A. M. Weather bright and clear; business very big. The large horse tent was set on fire by a spark from the engine and was almost entirely destroyed.</p>
         <p>Lot—Market and Broad streets.</p>
         <p>Arena—153 x 328.</p>
      </div>

      <div class=" ">
         <h4>Fri. 26</h4>
         <h4>Reading, Pa.</h4>
         <h4>P. &amp; R. 35.</h4>
         <p>Arrived early. Weather clear; very large attendance at both performances. Mike Quinlan returns from the hospital at Springfield, O.</p>
         <p>Lot—10th and Berne streets.</p>
         <p>Arena—182 x 389.</p>
      </div>

      <div class=" ">
         <h4>Sat. 27</h4>
         <h4>Chester, Pa.</h4>
         <h4>P. &amp; R. 68.</h4>
         <p>Arrived 6.00 A. M., half-mile haul to lot. Weather clear and very warm; business light. To-night finishes the 100th performance of the season. Johnnie Baker injures his hand and is compelled to omit his shooting act.</p>
         <p>Lot—7th Street and Edgemont Avenue.</p>
         <p>Arena—157 x 341.</p>
      </div>

      <h6 class="fw">May-June.</h6>

      <div class=" ">
         <h4>Mon. 29</h4>
         <h4>Philadelphia, Pa.</h4>
         <h4>P. &amp; R. 12.</h4>
         <p>Arrived here about 5.00 A. M. Sunday was spent painting the poles, etc., thus giving the show a brighter appearance. The weather for the opening day proved clear and warm, and a large attendance was on hand. Managers Jas. A. Bailey, Nate Salsbury, and W. W. Cole paid a business visit.</p>
      </div>

      <div class=" ">
         <h4>Tues. 30</h4>
         <p>Tuesday, Decoration Day, brings out a large attendance twice; weather clear.</p>
      </div>

      <div class=" ">
         <h4>Wed. 31</h4>
         <div class="note">No entry</div>
      </div>

      <div class=" ">
         <h4>Thur. 1</h4>
         <p>Thursday evening, a wind and rain storm threatened to break up the performance, but soon cleared off.</p>
      </div>

      <div class=" ">
         <h4>Fri. 2</h4>
         <p>Friday extra reserved seats were put in, to accommodate the large crowd in the evening.</p>
      </div>

      <div class=" ">
         <h4>Sat. 3</h4>
         <p>Saturday, weather continues clear and two good houses mark the closing day here. Fred Randel, one of the cooks, fell from car platform, while we were pulling out for Long Branch, and had his right foot cut off; he was taken to the hospital in Philadelphia.</p>
         <p>Lot—29th and Columbia.</p>
         <p>Arena—165 x 329.</p>
      </div>

      <h6 class="fw">June.</h6>

      <div class=" ">
         <h4>Mon. 5</h4>
         <h4>Long Branch, N. J.</h4>
         <h4>P. R. R. 94.</h4>
         <p>Arrived 6.30 A. M. Two-mile haul to the lot, which is very dusty. Weather clear and warm; very large attendance at evening performance. Jack Joyce has a fall in the "Race of Races," and is badly bruised up.</p>
         <p>Lot—Riverside and Atlantic avenues.</p>
         <p>Arena—170 x 349.</p>
      </div>

      <div class=" ">
         <h4>Tues. 6</h4>
         <h4>Elizabeth, N. J.</h4>
         <h4>P. R. R. 35.</h4>
         <p>Arrived 7.00 A. M. Two miles to lot. Weather very hot; night attendance very big. Tom Dennis, an English lancer, sent to the hospital with a broken collar bone.</p>
         <p>Lot—Third Avenue and Spencer Street.</p>
         <p>Arena—166 x 365.</p>
      </div>

      <div class=" ">
         <h4>Wed. 7</h4>
         <h4>Yonkers, N. Y.</h4>
         <h4>P. R. R. and N. Y. C. 35.</h4>
         <p>Second section did not get in till 10.00 A. M., having been delayed at the ferry. Lot very small. Cook-tent and horse-tent about one half mile from the rest of the show. Weather very hot.</p>
         <p>Lot—Monastery and Palisade avenues.</p>
         <p>Arena—153 x 316.</p>
      </div>

      <div class=" ">
         <h4>Thur. 8</h4>
         <h4>Poughkeepsie, N. Y.</h4>
         <h4>N. Y. C. 58.</h4>
         <p>Arrrived 6.30 A. M. Two miles to lot. Weather clear; business light. Jack Reilly, a driver, fell from a wagon, breaking his leg; he was taken to the hospital here.</p>
         <p>Lot—Darrow Park.</p>
         <p>Arena—120 x 352.</p>
      </div>

      <div class=" ">
         <h4>Fri. 9</h4>
         <h4>Winsted, Ct.</h4>
         <h4>C. N. E. 80.</h4>
         <p>Arrived 7.30 A. M. Lot close to crossing, and in very bad condition. Weather cloudy; business fair.</p>
         <p>Lot—Willow Street.</p>
         <p>Arena—112 x 334.</p>
      </div>

      <div class=" ">
         <h4>Sat. 10</h4>
         <h4>Hartford, Ct.</h4>
         <h4>C. N. E. 35.</h4>
         <p>Arrived 6.00 A. M. Unloaded close to lot. Weather clear; big business at both performances. The lot shows the tracks left by us last season, and is very rough.</p>
         <p>Lot—Gentlemen's Driving Park.</p>
         <p>Arena—176 x 394.</p>
      </div>
      <h6 class="fw">31</h6>

      <span class="hr"> </span>
      <span class="pageimage">
         <a href="large/wfc.route.1899.037.jpg"
            rel="prettyPhoto[pp_gal]"
            title="&lt;a href=&#34;large/wfc.route.1899.037.jpg&#34; target=&#34;_blank&#34; &gt;open image in new window&lt;/a&gt;">
            <img src="thumbnails/wfc.route.1899.037.jpg" class="display &#xA;            "/>
         </a>

      <h6 class="fw">June.</h6>

      <div class=" ">
         <h4>Mon. 12</h4>
         <h4>Boston, Mass.</h4>
         <h4>N. Y, N. H. &amp; H. and B. &amp; A. 131.</h4>
         <p>Arrived in town at noon Sunday, after a very slow and tedious run. A special grandstand had been erected in place of our usual reserved seats. </p>
         <p>Monday opened in fair weather, to two good houses.</p>
      </div>

      <div class=" ">
         <h4>Tues. 13</h4>
         <h4>Wed. 14</h4>
         <p>Tuesday and Wednesday the weather was warm and clear, and the attendance large at each performance.</p>
      </div>

      <div class=" ">
         <h4>Thurs. 15</h4>
         <p>Thursday we had a wet day, and the attendance fell off a little on this account. Visits were exchanged with the Pawnee Wild West play at Waltham.</p>
      </div>

      <div class=" ">
         <h4>Fri. 16</h4>
         <p>Friday, clear weather brings out a large crowd, and extra seats had to be put up for the night performance.</p>
      </div>

      <div class=" ">
         <h4>Sat. 17</h4>
         <p>Saturday, the closing day here, the two performances were given to good houses. Weather clear. Pony Moore returns from New York and resumes his work in the artillery detachment.</p>
         <p>Lot—Huntingdon Avenue Grounds.</p>
         <p>Arena—176 x 346.</p>
      </div>
      <h6 class="fw">32</h6>

      <span class="hr"> </span>
      <span class="pageimage">

      <h6 class="fw">June.</h6>

      <div class=" ">
         <h4>Mon. 19</h4>
         <h4>Brocton, Mass.</h4>
         <h4>N.Y., N. H. &amp; H. 20.</h4>
         <p>Arrived early. Lot three miles from crossing. Weather warm and clear; big business at both performances.</p>
         <p>Lot—Torrey and Belmont streets.</p>
         <p>Arena—174 x 303.</p>
      </div>

      <div class=" ">
         <h4>Tues. 20</h4>
         <h4>New Bedford, Mass.</h4>
         <h4>N. Y., N. H. &amp; H. 31.</h4>
         <p>Arrived 6.30 A. M. Two miles to lot. Weather clear; good business at both performances.</p>
         <p>Lot—Acushnet Avenue.</p>
         <p>Arena—162 x 342.</p>
      </div>

      <div class=" ">
         <h4>Wed. 21</h4>
         <h4>Newport, R. I.</h4>
         <h4>N. Y., N. H. &amp; H. 41.</h4>
         <p>Arrived 6.00 A. M. An axle on the first section stock car broke and the car had to be left behind. Weather clear; good house at night.</p>
         <p>Lot—Thames and Harrison streets.</p>
         <p>Arena—171 x 342.</p>
      </div>

      <div class=" ">
         <h4>Thur. 22</h4>
         <h4>Fall River, Mass.</h4>
         <h4>N. Y., N. H. &amp; H. 18.</h4>
         <p>Arrived 5.30. Half-mile haul to lot. Weather clear; business fair. Pete Wallace, porter of car 54, was badly hurt by a fall from a moving train.</p>
         <p>Lot—Broadway and Centre Street.</p>
         <p>Arena—166 x 337.</p>
      </div>

      <div class=" ">
         <h4>Fri. 23</h4>
         <h4>New London, Ct.</h4>
         <h4>N. Y., N. H. &amp; H. 84.</h4>
         <p>Arrived 9.00 A. M. The parade was given and the doors opened on time. Weather cool; good attendance at both performances.</p>
         <p>Lot—Ball Grounds.</p>
         <p>Arena—167 x 334.</p>
      </div>

      <div class=" ">
         <h4>Sat. 24</h4>
         <h4>Willimantic, Ct.</h4>
         <h4>C. Vt. 30.</h4>
         <p>Arrived 7.00 A. M. Half mile to lot, which proves to be very soft. Heavy rain during afternoon; business fair.</p>
         <p>Lot—Fair Grounds.</p>
         <p>Arena—165 x 315.</p>
      </div>

      <h6 class="fw">June-July.</h6>

      <div class=" ">
         <h4>Mon. 26</h4>
         <h4>Bridgeport, Ct.</h4>
         <h4>N. Y., N. H. &amp; H. 72.</h4>
         <p>Arrived 5.00 A. M. A heavy rain all Sunday puts the lot in pretty bad shape, but a clear, warm day on Monday brings an enormous attendance at both performances. Johnnie Baker resumes his shooting act.</p>
         <p>Lot—Winterquarters.</p>
         <p>Arena—145 x 317.</p>
      </div>

      <div class=" ">
         <h4>Tues. 27</h4>
         <h4>Waterbury, Ct.</h4>
         <h4>N. Y., N. H. &amp; H. 32.</h4>
         <p>Arrived 5.00 A. M. One-mile haul to lot. Weather clear. The lot is situated quarter of a mile from the street; business very big.</p>
         <p>Lot—West Main Street</p>
         <p>Arena—314 x 172.</p>
      </div>

      <div class=" ">
         <h4>Wed. 28</h4>
         <h4>New Haven, Ct.</h4>
         <h4>N. Y., N. H. &amp; H. 30.</h4>
         <p>Arrived early. Three-mile haul to lot. Rain during afternoon, clear at night; very large attendance at evening performance.</p>
         <p>Lot—Foot of Elm Street.</p>
         <p>Arena—172 x 325.</p>
      </div>

      <div class=" ">
         <h4>Thur. 29</h4>
         <h4>Holyoke, Mass.</h4>
         <h4>N. Y., N. H. &amp; H. 62.</h4>
         <p>Arrived 6.30, and unloaded close to lot. Weather clear; good attendance at both performances.</p>
         <p>Lot—Depot Hill.</p>
         <p>Arena—180 x 338.</p>
      </div>

      <div class=" ">
         <h4>Fri. 30</h4>
         <h4>Springfield, Mass.</h4>
         <h4>B. &amp; M. 8.</h4>
         <p>Arrived early and unloaded close to park. Weather clear; business big. Rough Rider McGinty has a fall and is badly shaken up.</p>
         <p>Lot—Hampden Park.</p>
         <p>Arena—162 x 345.</p>
      </div>

      <div class=" ">
         <h4>Sat. 1</h4>
         <h4>Worcester, Mass.</h4>
         <h4>B. &amp; A. 55.</h4>
         <p>Arrived 6.00 A. M. One-mile haul to lot. Weather clear; large attendance at both performances.</p>
         <p>Lot—Grove and Morgan streets.</p>
         <p>Arena—124 x 358.</p>
      </div>

      <h6 class="fw">July.</h6>

      <div class=" ">
         <h4>Mon. 3</h4>
         <h4>Salem, Mass.</h4>
         <h4>B. &amp; A. and B. &amp; M. 60.</h4>
         <p>Arrived early. One-mile haul to lot. Weather clear and very warm; business big at both performances.</p>
         <p>Lot—Bridge Street.</p>
         <p>Arena—154 x 388.</p>
      </div>

      <div class=" ">
         <h4>Tues. 4</h4>
         <h4>Lawrence, Mass.</h4>
         <h4>B. &amp; M. 24.</h4>
         <p>Arrived 4.30 A. M. Lot three-fourths mile from crossing. Weather clear and warm; big business. The cook tent was tastefully decorated, and our caterers, Messrs. Keen &amp; Langan, prepared a special supper in honor of the Fourth, which was greatly appreciated by all.</p>
         <p>Lot—Merrimac Street.</p>
         <p>Arena—162 x 345.</p>
      </div>

      <div class=" ">
         <h4>Wed. 5</h4>
         <h4>Haverhill, Mass.</h4>
         <h4>B. &amp; M. 7.</h4>
         <p>Arrived 5.00 A. M. One-mile haul to lot. Weather clear; business big.</p>
         <p>Lot—River Street.</p>
         <p>Arena—162 x 345.</p>
      </div>

      <div class=" ">
         <h4>Thur. 6</h4>
         <h4>Dover, N. H.</h4>
         <h4>B. &amp; M. 35.</h4>
         <p>Arrived 4.30 A. M. Lot a mile and a half from crossing. Weather clear; business big at both performances.</p>
         <p>Lot—Silver Street.</p>
         <p>Arena—153 x 368.</p>
      </div>

      <div class=" ">
         <h4>Fri. 7</h4>
         <h4>Concord, N. H.</h4>
         <h4>B. &amp; M. 61.</h4>
         <p>Arrived 6.30 A. M. Half mile to lot. Weather clear; attendance big at both performances.</p>
         <p>Lot—Three Bridge Road.</p>
         <p>Arena—147 x 353.</p>
      </div>

      <div class=" ">
         <h4>Sat. 8</h4>
         <h4>Manchester, N. H.</h4>
         <h4>B. &amp; M. 18.</h4>
         <p>Arrived 4.30 A. M. One-mile haul to lot. Heavy rain all day; business fair.</p>
         <p>Lot—Valley and Maple streets.</p>
         <p>Arena—174 x 375.</p>
      </div>

         <h4>Mon. 10</h4>
         <h4>Lowell, Mass.</h4>
         <h4>B. &amp; M. 31.</h4>
         <p>Arrived early. Lot one mile from crossing. Rain on Sunday followed by a clear day Monday: business good.</p>
         <p>Lot—Fair Grounds.</p>
         <p>Arena—160 x 384.</p>
      </div>

      <div class=" ">
         <h4>Tues. 11</h4>
         <h4>Fitchburg, Mass.</h4>
         <h4>N. Y., N. H. &amp; H. 66.</h4>
         <p>Arrived 6.00 A. M. Weather clear; business big at both performances. Frank Read, assistant boss hostler, closes and his place is given to Frank McNall.</p>
         <p>Lot—Ball Grounds.</p>
         <p>Arena—145 x 349.</p>
      </div>

      <div class=" ">
         <h4>Wed. 12</h4>
         <h4>Greenfield, Mass.</h4>
         <h4>Fitchburg. 55.</h4>
         <p>Arrived early. One mile to lot. Thunderstorm during afternoon; business fair.</p>
         <p>Lot—Federal and Silver streets.</p>
         <p>Arena—167 x 336.</p>
      </div>

      <div class=" ">
         <h4>Thur. 13</h4>
         <h4>Saratoga, N. Y.</h4>
         <h4>Fitchburg and D. &amp; H. C. 101.</h4>
         <p>Arrived 7.30 A. M. One-mile haul to lot. Weather clear; business fair.</p>
         <p>Lot—Union and Nelson avenues.</p>
         <p>Arena—171 x 343.</p>
      </div>

      <div class=" ">
         <h4>Fri. 14</h4>
         <h4>Schenectady, N. Y.</h4>
         <h4>D. &amp; H. C. 22.</h4>
         <p>Arrived 4.30 A. M. Lot one mile from crossing. Weather clear; business good.</p>
         <p>Lot—Driving Park.</p>
         <p>Arena—139 x 358.</p>
      </div>

      <div class=" ">
         <h4>Sat. 15</h4>
         <h4>Utica, N. Y.</h4>
         <h4>N. Y. C. &amp; H. R. 78.</h4>
         <p>Arrived 5.00 A. M. Unloaded close to lot. Weather clear; business very big. Sergt. Webb of the Rough Riders is sent to hospital here.</p>
         <p>Lot—Foot of Meadow Street.</p>
         <p>Arena—154 x 336.</p>
      </div>
      <h6 class="fw">36</h6>

      <span class="hr"> </span>
      <span class="pageimage">

      <h6 class="fw">July.</h6>

      <div class=" ">
         <h4>Mon. 17</h4>
         <h4>Syracuse, N. Y.</h4>
         <h4>N. Y. C. &amp; H. R. 41.</h4>
         <p>Arrived early. Heavy rain all day Sunday, followed by a clear, warm day Monday; business big. Albert Zimes of the band injures his leg and is compelled to go to the hospital. Archie Clements also goes to the hospital, with a mild case of typhoid.</p>
         <p>Lot—Kirk Park.</p>
         <p>Arena—151 x 344.</p>
      </div>

      <div class=" ">
         <h4>Tues. 18</h4>
         <h4>Binghamton, N. Y.</h4>
         <h4>D., L. &amp; W. 79.</h4>
         <p>Arrived 7.00 A. M. Half-mile to lot. Weather clear; business big.</p>
         <p>Lot—Ball Grounds.</p>
         <p>Arena—169 x 356.</p>
      </div>

      <div class=" ">
         <h4>Wed. 19</h4>
         <h4>Elmira, N. Y.</h4>
         <h4>D., L. &amp; W. 57.</h4>
         <p>Arrived 5:00 A. M. Two-mile haul to lot. Weather clear; business big. During the night performance a lady fell from the seats, breaking her leg.</p>
         <p>Lot—Fair Grounds.</p>
         <p>Arena—171 x 343.</p>
      </div>

      <div class=" ">
         <h4>Thur. 20</h4>
         <h4>Rochester, N. Y.</h4>
         <h4>Erie. 112.</h4>
         <p>Arrived 7.30 A. M. Two miles to lot; business immense at both performances.</p>
         <p>Lot—Driving Park.</p>
         <p>Arena—217 x 400.</p>
      </div>

      <div class=" ">
         <h4>Fri. 21 and Sat. 22</h4>
         <h4>Buffalo, N. Y.</h4>
         <h4>N. Y. C. &amp; H. R. 67.</h4>
         <p>Arrived early. A heavy rain during afternoon puts the lot in very bad condition; however, the tent was filled at both performances Friday. Saturday, weather clear; business very big. Many members of the company visit the Falls.</p>
         <p>Lot—Driving Park.</p>
         <p>Arena—178 x 402.</p>
      </div>
      <h6 class="fw">37</h6>

      <span class="hr"> </span>
      <span class="pageimage">
         <a href="large/wfc.route.1899.043.jpg"
            rel="prettyPhoto[pp_gal]"
            title="&lt;a href=&#34;large/wfc.route.1899.043.jpg&#34; target=&#34;_blank&#34; &gt;open image in new window&lt;/a&gt;">

      <h6 class="fw">July.</h6>

      <div class=" ">
         <h4>Mon. 24</h4>
         <h4>Cleveland, O.</h4>
         <h4>L. S. &amp; M. S. 183.</h4>
         <p>Arrived 10.30 Sunday. Weather clear; business very big; doors closed at night. Jack Dawson fell and fractured his ankle; he was taken to the hospital here. </p>
         <p>Lot—Payne Avenue and Oliver Street.</p>
         <p>Arena—188 x 392.</p>
      </div>

      <div class=" ">
         <h4>Tues. 25</h4>
         <h4>Akron, O.</h4>
         <h4>C. T. &amp; V. 35.</h4>
         <p>Arrived 6.30 A. M. Half-mile haul. A heavy thunderstorm came up during the afternoon, but cleared off at night; business very big.</p>
         <p>Lot—Thornton Street and Boulevard.</p>
         <p>Arena—159 x 343.</p>
      </div>

      <div class=" ">
         <h4>Wed. 26</h4>
         <h4>Canton, O.</h4>
         <h4>C. T. &amp; V. 14.</h4>
         <p>Arrived 5.00 A. M. Tableau wagon No. 100 was upset near the runs, delaying the work a little. Weather very hot; business big.</p>
         <p>Lot—E. Tarwas Street.</p>
         <p>Arena—166 X 337.</p>
      </div>

      <div class=" ">
         <h4>Thur. 27</h4>
         <h4>Youngstown, O.</h4>
         <h4>P. R. R. 55.</h4>
         <p>Arrived early. Two miles to lot. Weather warm and clear; business big. Johnnie Baker loses his pocket-book, containing $240 and a valuable diamond pin, a gift of the colonel.</p>
         <p>Lot—Opposite Fair Grounds.</p>
         <p>Arena—175 x 343.</p>
      </div>

      <div class=" ">
         <h4>Fri. 28</h4>
         <h4>Beaver Falls, Pa.</h4>
         <h4>P. R. R. 35.</h4>
         <p>Arrived early. Weather very hot; business big. A five-gallon can of gasolene exploded in car 56. Ed Sullivan, the porter, and Jas. Parker, a canvasman, were very badly burned, and the car was totally destroyed; the injured men were taken to the hospital here.</p>
         <p>Lot—Fourth Avenue and 33d Street.</p>
         <p>Arena—173 x 353.</p>
      </div>

      <div class=" ">
         <h4>Sat. 29</h4>
         <h4>Stuebenville, O.</h4>
         <h4>P.R.R. 50.</h4>
         <p>First section arrived 5.00 A. M., the second did not get in till 9.00 A.M. A squall of wind struck the show about 6.30 P. M., but passed over without much damage.</p>
         <p>Lot—Pleasant Heights.</p>
         <p>Arena—178 x 356.</p>
      </div>
      <h6 class="fw">38</h6>

      <span class="hr"> </span>
      <span class="pageimage">
         <a href="large/wfc.route.1899.044.jpg"
            rel="prettyPhoto[pp_gal]"
            title="&lt;a href=&#34;large/wfc.route.1899.044.jpg&#34; target=&#34;_blank&#34; &gt;open image in new window&lt;/a&gt;">
            <img src="thumbnails/wfc.route.1899.044.jpg" class="display &#xA;            "/>
         </a>
      </span>

      <h6 class="fw">July-August.</h6>

      <div class=" ">
         <h4>Mon. 31</h4>
         <h4>Coshocton, O.</h4>
         <h4>P.R.R. 81.</h4>
         <p>Arrived 6.30 A. M. Weather clear; business good. A ball game was played between a Wild West Nine and the local club yesterday, resulting in a sweeping victory for the Wild West. Score: 14 to 0.</p>
         <p>Lot—E. Main and 11th streets.</p>
         <p>Arena—168 x 352.</p>
      </div>

      <div class=" ">
         <h4>Tues. 1</h4>
         <h4>Mansfield, O.</h4>
         <h4>P. R. R. 78.</h4>
         <p>Arrived early. Very soft lot. Weather clear; very big afternoon house. Fred Essex of the band closes. </p>
         <p>Lot—3d and Ashland streets.</p>
         <p>Arena—163 x 348.</p>
      </div>

      <div class=" ">
         <h4>Wed. 3</h4>
         <h4>Upper Sandusky, O.</h4>
         <h4>P. R. R. 78.</h4>
         <p>Arrived 5.00 A. M. One-mile haul to lot. Weather clear; business fair. J. McAdams joins the band. </p>
         <p>Lot—E. Bigelow street.</p>
         <p>Arena—162 x 347.</p>
      </div>

      <div class=" ">
         <h4>Thur. 3</h4>
         <h4>Lima, O.</h4>
         <h4>P. R. R. 44.</h4>
         <p>Arrived early. One mile to lot; big business. A heavy thunderstorm came up during evening. Miller of the Rough Riders is taken to the hospital with typhoid. Sergeant Webb returns from hospital at Utica.</p>
         <p>Lot—Vine Street.</p>
         <p>Arena—166 x 348.</p>
      </div>

      <div class=" ">
         <h4>Fri. 4</h4>
         <h4>Muncie, Ind.</h4>
         <h4>L. E. &amp; W. 85</h4>
         <p>Arrived 6.30. A heavy rainstorm, accompanied with thunder and lightning, keeps the lot in bad shape; business fair. Fred Hoffman (Fritz) is sent to the hospital with a broken leg.</p>
         <p>Lot—Weiser and Madison streets.</p>
         <p>Arena—174 x 382.</p>
      </div>

      <div class=" ">
         <h4>Sat. 5</h4>
         <h4>Fort Wayne, Ind.</h4>
         <h4>L. E. &amp; W. 65.</h4>
         <p>Arrived early. Lot two miles from town; immense business; doors closed. Little Mary, Indian papoose, died suddenly here.</p>
         <p>Lot—Lakeside.</p>
         <p>Arena—165 x 383.</p>
      </div>
      <h6 class="fw">39</h6>

      <span class="hr"> </span>
      <span class="pageimage">
         <a href="large/wfc.route.1899.045.jpg"
            rel="prettyPhoto[pp_gal]"
            title="&lt;a href=&#34;large/wfc.route.1899.045.jpg&#34; target=&#34;_blank&#34; &gt;open image in new window&lt;/a&gt;">

         </a>

      <h6 class="fw">August.</h6>
      <div class=" ">
         <h4>Mon. 7</h4>
         <h4>Hillsdale, Mich.</h4>
         <h4>L. S. &amp; M. S. 71.</h4>
         <p>Arrived 9.00 A. M. Half-mile haul to lot. Weather clear; business very big in afternoon, fair at night. Three of the Arabs close.</p>
         <p>Lot—Howell Street.</p>
         <p>Arena—173 x 350.</p>
      </div>

      <div class=" ">
         <h4>Tues. 8</h4>
         <h4>Jackson, Mich.</h4>
         <h4>L. S. &amp; M. S. 26.</h4>
         <p>Arrived early. One-mile haul. Weather clear; business very big. A new sleeping car arrived, to take the place of one destroyed at Beaver Falls.</p>
         <p>Lot—Fair Grounds.</p>
         <p>Arena—168 x 352.</p>
      </div>

      <div class=" ">
         <h4>Wed. 9</h4>
         <h4>Lansing, Mich.</h4>
         <h4>M. C. 36.</h4>
         <p>Arrived 6.00 A. M. A mile and a half haul. Weather clear; business big. Ed Lacey of the Forepaugh-Sells Show pays us a visit.</p>
         <p>Lot—Fair Grounds.</p>
         <p>Arena—166 x 349.</p>
      </div>

      <div class=" ">
         <h4>Thur. 10</h4>
         <h4>Bay City, Mich.</h4>
         <h4>M. C. 79.</h4>
         <p>Arrived 6.30 A. M. One-mile haul to lot. Weather clear; business big.</p>
         <p>Lot—Fair Grounds.</p>
         <p>Arena—178 x 379.</p>
      </div>

      <div class=" ">
         <h4>Fri. 11</h4>
         <h4>Port Huron, Mich.</h4>
         <h4>F. &amp; P. M. 102.</h4>
         <p>Arrived 7.30 A. M. A wind storm struck the show about 1.30 P. M. and blew down the front end. However, things were soon straightened out, and the show went on a usual; business big.</p>
         <p>Lot—Lapeer Avenue.</p>
         <p>Arena—176 x 383.</p>
      </div>

      <div class=" ">
         <h4>Sat. 12</h4>
         <h4>Detroit, Mich.</h4>
         <h4>G. T. R. 58.</h4>
         <p>Arrived early. Three-quarter-mile haul. Weather clear. Lot very hard and rough. One of the Filipinos has a fall, and is badly shaken up. Flat Iron returns from hospital at Utica.</p>
         <p>Lot—Grand River Ave. and Hudson St.</p>
         <p>Arena—178 x 388.</p>
      </div>
      <h6 class="fw">40</h6>

      <span class="hr"> </span>
      <span class="pageimage">
         <a href="large/wfc.route.1899.046.jpg"

      <h6 class="fw">41</h6>

      <span class="hr"> </span>
      <span class="pageimage">
         <a href="large/wfc.route.1899.047.jpg"
            rel="prettyPhoto[pp_gal]"
            title="&lt;a href=&#34;large/wfc.route.1899.047.jpg&#34; target=&#34;_blank&#34; &gt;open image in new window&lt;/a&gt;">

      <h6 class="fw">August.</h6>
      <div class=" ">
         <h4>Mon. 21—Tues. 22—Wed. 23—Thur. 24— Fri. 25—Sat. 26—Sun. 27</h4>
         <h4>Chicago, Ill.—C., R. I. &amp; P. 161.</h4>

         <p>We reached here at 6.00 A. M., after an exceptionally fast run from Peoria.</p>

         <p>A grand stand had been erected, to take the place of our regular reserved seats. The Battle Scene was also greatly strengthened by fifty additional men, and the erection of a much larger hill than that used on the road.</p>

         <p>The weather during the entire week was warm and clear, and the business tremendous—there being thousands turned away every evening.</p>

         <p>On Friday, August 25th, it was found necessary to put in the extra forty-five foot middle piece, in order to put up more seats to accommodate the crowds.</p>

         <p>There were fourteen performances given during our stay here, which terminated on Sunday evening, August 27th.</p>

         <p>A large number of the show employés closed here during the week.</p>

         <p>Lot—35th Street and Wentworth Ave.</p>
         <p>Arena—163 x 398.</p>
      </div>

      <div class=" ">
         <h4>Home, Sweet Home.</h4>
      </div>

      <h6 class="fw">49</h6>
   </div>
   <span class="hr"> </span>
   <span class="pageimage">
      <a href="large/wfc.route.1899.055.jpg"
         rel="prettyPhoto[pp_gal]"
         title="&lt;a href=&#34;large/wfc.route.1899.055.jpg&#34; target=&#34;_blank&#34; &gt;open image in new window&lt;/a&gt;">
         <img src="thumbnails/wfc.route.1899.055.jpg" class="display &#xA;            "/>
      </a>
   </span>

   <div class=" doublespace ">
      <div class=" ">
         <h4>A Few Statistics.</h4>

         <p>Starting from Bridgeport, Ct., on April 14th, the "Wild West" traveled a distance of 11,111 miles, using the tracks of forty different railroads.</p>

         <p>The show was on the road 200 days, during which time 341 performances were given, 132 towns visited in twenty-four States, viz: one stand of two and one-half weeks, four one-week stands, five two-day, and 122 one-day, on seven of which only one performance was given.</p>

         <p>There were 529 people employed in all departments, the "Wild West" stable contained 325 horses, and the baggage stock numbered 119 head. The shortest run from one stand to the next was seven miles, from Lawrence, Mass., to Haverill, the longest, 205 miles, from Kirksville, Mo., to St. Louis.</p>

         <p>For transportation purposes the show used thirty-five baggage wagons, two band wagons, two water tanks, two engines for electric light, four buggies, two field pieces and caissons and one Gatling gun. The trains consisted of sixteen flat cars, fifteen stock cars and eight sleeping coaches. The show carried eighty lengths of blue seats and eleven sections of reserved seats, giving seating accommodation to approximately 13,000 people.</p>
      </div>

      <div class=" ">
         <h4>Past Seasons with the Wild West.</h4>


         <h5>1883.</h5>
         <p>The Buffalo Bill Wild West Show was organized as an outdoor show in 1883, and opened in Omaha, Neb., in May, and traveled through the States of Nebraska, Iowa, Illinois, Kentucky, Indiana, Pennsylvania, New York, Connecticut, Massachusetts and Rhode Island, giving the performance in 
<span class="h6">50</span>

            <span class="hr"> </span>
            <span class="pageimage">
               <a href="large/wfc.route.1899.056.jpg"
                  rel="prettyPhoto[pp_gal]"
                  title="&lt;a href=&#34;large/wfc.route.1899.056.jpg&#34; target=&#34;_blank&#34; &gt;open image in new window&lt;/a&gt;">
                  <img src="thumbnails/wfc.route.1899.056.jpg" class="display &#xA;            "/>
               </a>
            </span>

Fair Grounds with the exception of Coney Island, where a temporary stand was erected, and they remained there five weeks. It was at this place that the first horse race was ever given by electric light.</p>




         <h5>1884-5.</h5>
         <p>Opened in May, in St. Louis, Mo., went through the Eastern States and Canada. October 31st took a boat down the Mississippi River, bound for New Orleans. The boat was wrecked at Rodney, Miss., and everything was lost except horses. Opened in New Orleans Christmas week, and closed April 1, 1885, then worked north through the Central and Southern States, including Michigan and Wisconsin, and closed October 31st at St. Louis, Mo.</p>


         <h5>1886.</h5>
         <p>Opened in St. Louis in May, and then played through to New York, where they opened a season at Erastina, Staten Island, in June, and remained until September 30th, then opened a winter season at Madison Square Garden, Thanksgiving Eve, and closed Washington's Birthday, 1887. During their stay at the Garden they lost sixteen buffaloes, from lung trouble.</p>


         <h5>1887.</h5>
         <p>April 1st, sailed on the steamer "State of Nebraska" for London, England, where they remained a season of six months, and then went to Manchester, England, for six months, and closed April 30, 1888; then gave one performance at Hull, England, in the afternoon, and sailed the same night for New York City on the steamer "Persian Monarch."</p>


         <h5>1888.</h5>
         <p>Opened the season at Erastina, Staten Island, on Decoration Day, and remained six

<span class="h6">51</span>

            <span class="hr"> </span>
            <span class="pageimage">
               <a href="large/wfc.route.1899.057.jpg"
                  rel="prettyPhoto[pp_gal]"
                  title="&lt;a href=&#34;large/wfc.route.1899.057.jpg&#34; target=&#34;_blank&#34; &gt;open image in new window&lt;/a&gt;">
                  <img src="thumbnails/wfc.route.1899.057.jpg" class="display &#xA;            "/>
               </a>
            </span>

weeks; then went to Philadelphia, Baltimore and Washington, and closed at the State Fair in Richmond, Va., October 22d.</p>


         <h5>1889-90.</h5>
         <p>Sailed April 12th on the Steamer "Persian Monarch" for Havre, France, where a season of six months was played at Paris. They then toured through France, Spain, Italy, Germany and Austria, and closed in the City of Strasburg, Alsace-Lorraine, October 29, 1890. Some of the troupe returned to the United States, while others remained there.</p>


         <h5>1891-2.</h5>
         <p>Opened in Stuttgart, April 15th, and played through Germany, Belgium and England; closed at Croyden, England, October 31st. Opened again at Glasgow, Scotland, November 15th, and remained until April 15, 1892. May 9th opened again in London, and closed October 27, 1892, and sailed on the Steamer "Mohawk," October 29th, for New York City.</p>


         <h5>1893.</h5>
         <p>This was the World's Fair season. There was a Grand Stand erected at 62d and 63d streets and Grace Avenue, Chicago, with a seating capacity of 20,000 people. It was opened April 26th, and closed October 31st, making 186 days of continuous performance; not one show was missed, and it closed the most successful season known in show history.</p>


         <h5>1894.</h5>
         <p>Opened in Ambrose Park, Brooklyn, N. Y., May 12th, and closed October 6th. One show was missed September 14th, on account of heavy rain; no Sunday shows were given, making a run of 126 days.</p>

         <h6 class="fw">52</h6>
      </div>
   </div>
